text:
This is a great sausage gravy with any type of sausage. Maple tastes great & I normally wouldn't have chosen it, but have used it several times for this gravy. I end up having to use a little extra flour because I make this with 1% milk, which is what I normally buy. OH - ONE OTHER THING: The most popular review states that he whisks the milk & flour together & adds it to the sausage directly. The reason the recipe is written the way it is - is because you need to cook the flour in the drippings & butter to get rid of the "floury" taste. All successful white sauces are made this way. Following the original recipe as written makes the best tasting gravy!

text:
We love this recipe!  However I did tweek it a little bit so that I could get the taste closer to that of which they serve at the Montage in Portland, OR.  I add about 4 Tablespoons of maple syrup after it thickens and 1/4 teaspoon cayenne pepper OR replace maple sausage with chorizo sausage to make it spicy....but you can add either to your liking, I just found that it makes the flavor burst!  Also, I serve mine over buttermilk biscuits...the only way to eat them!  Thanks Bill!

This is a fine, kick-butt recipe, but for me NOT with maple sausage.  This must be a regional thing.  I was introduced to B&G in the southwest- I must've tried 10 different versions while going through Texas, alone.  But none of them used maple sausage and most of them were heavily peppered.  So I just use a sage or other standard breakfast sausage (but not hot sausage) and am heavy-handed with the black pepper.  The fresh-made country breakfast sausage available at Sprouts was quite good in this- they also have a maple sausage if you must have it, but please try it with a regular sausage before you tell me I'm all wet.  Enjoy it with strong black coffee for that true truck-stop feeling.  

Thanks kindly for reading...

text:
One of my favorite things to eat. Been making cream/milk gravy since my mother in law taught me how in 1974. Season with salt and pepper. The only thing I added salt to when I was pregnant.  This is the same recipe basically I've used since then. Tweek it however suits you. The meat doesn't matter, the extras don't matter, it's what appeals to you. Use on biscuits, toast, plain bread or right on the meat. I've made it with sausage patties, ground sausage, bacon, pork chops, hamburger, kielbasa, country fried steak and after frying chicken.  YUM!!!! My son in law adds tabasco at the table. I've gone from whole milk to 2% to 1% and it's a winner with any of them.  I only take the meat out if it's not ground, then cover with the flour and brown a bit. It's really not necessary to brown it for very long. The important advise I'll give is to not walk away from it after you put the milk. It will probably stick if you don't. But I don't simmer it, also don't use high heat,  so I stir as it cooks. Best to keep it moving. But it won't take long. It might also get a little thicker after it's done. But it generally doesn't sit around too long. Only thing I don't do is add butter. If I need a bit more drippings I add a little shortening or oil if I have to stretch the drippings a bit and keep the meat flavor.  Don't need to do this often but it's not a heart friendly thing to begin with. Otherwise it would be on the table everyday. *L*

text:
This is a wonderful recipe! Make as written first! My tips are as follows:
1) I use 1 lb regular breakfast sausage (Jimmy Deans is always good or in bulk from our local butcher)
2) We don't buy whole milk, so I use 2 cups nonfat milk and then the last cup I mix 1/2 c. nonfat with 1/2 c. half and half. But I must say all nonfat turns out just fine.
3) 2 T of butter with the drippings is plent of fat. The extra just makes it that much richer, but I don't miss that.
4) I strongly encourge you to add the flour to the fat as written in the recipe! This is a classic roux and this ensures the gravy doesn't taste "flour-y" or "pasty" -- mixing with the milk is a risk. Let the flour and drippings cook together, whisking constantly, about 1-2 minutes. This gives FLAVOR!
5) The milk/fat/flour ratio is perfect. I heat the milk in the microwave for about 1 minute so it's not too cold. Whisk in slowly. Once in, let come to a nice bubble and boil gently, stirring often. This thickens the gravy. Once you add the sausage and continue to cook, the thickening process continues. Thin with extra milk if too thick. As it cools, it will thicken more, so just add milk if needed.

Enjoy!!

This is a great basic sausage gravy recipe.  One tip and time saver I learned from my dad.  Don't bother to remove the sausage from the skillet.  Just add the flour to it & the drippings.  Cook for a few minutes till the flour browns and then add the milk.  It will thicken just fine and saves time & cleanup!

text:
Because of Bill, I will never again order biscuits and gravy in a restaurant! I have always loved B&G, but had never tried making it myself. This is so easy and just WOW. And it is absolutely because of the maple sausage. In my store, you can find regular pork sausage for much cheaper than the name brand maple sausage......so when I make this with regular sausage, I just add about 2 tbsps of maple syrup to the gravy after it is thickened. Although it isn't the same, it's close. Like a few others, I also make this with skim milk (because that's all we drink) and I omit the butter (you'd probably need the butter if you were using a leaner sausage, like turkey or chicken) - still turns out awesome and less fattening, too. Thank you, Bill! :)

text:
My family is Appalachian and I was raised on a farm eating biscuits and gravy, eggs and fried apples.  I tried this recipe because...well I'd never seen anyone "measure" a gravy recipe.  We are a dump and pour until it tastes right family.  My granny knew what she was talking about when she told me if you want the best tasting sausage gravy use bacon grease as the base and I have to agree.  I gave this a shot but it is much better if you reserve bacon grease to brown your flour in then add the drained sausage pieces to the gravy.  Also, for more punch try white pepper...everyone seems to forget about that little gem.

This is one of our family's favorites.  I've used maple sausage, and we all like it, but really prefer the plain stuff.  I usually don't have to add butter, and I sprinkle the flour right over the cooked sausage and stir it all together.  It's simpler than taking the sausage out of the pan, still gets the flour cooked, and works well.  This gravy is thick and flavorful, and our kids even ask for it for birthday breakfasts!

text:
Don't skimp on this recipe! All we had in the house was 1% milk, and turkey sausage. If you are already using 3T of butter don't hold back. it is still good as a lower fat version, but turkey is no sub. for good pork sausage! I also followed someone else's tip of adding some syrup directly to the gravy. YUM! I also like the idea of making the flour into a light rouge first. My mom always used a shaker and mixed the flour and milk before cooking which gives you a whiter gravy. But I do not have a shaker, so there was always a clump or two of flour in mine. The rouge adds nice flavor, and breaks down the flour for  a smoother gravy. Yum, going in my recipe box for sure! Thanks.

I'm not big on the maple sausage, but any flavor sausage will work well. Tip: After browning sausage, sprinkle flour directly over sausage and mix until the flour is no longer visible. Then add milk. No need to add butter. This makes it quick, easy,  and less fat with same flavor and texture.

text:
My mother is from Kentucky. Her mom, as well as my mom..and now me....have the secret to perfect gravy and the bland flavor this recipe and others may produce. Just add a little of your strong black coffee, one tbs. or a little more, at the end and stir in till well blended. It gives it a rich intense smokey (non coffee) taste and makes the gravy color a medium golden brown. It's an old pioneer trick farmer wives used when nothing was available to enhance their morning routine breakfast gravies. Enjoy! The instant aroma is even worth more. I also never remove the sausage (sage,regular) from the pan after it is browned. Also for truly velvet texture, my family only uses canned evaporated pet milk. Try serving this over lightly (sea)salted thick sliced (room temp) garden fresh tomatoes. Whewwww!!!  Kentucky Heaven! :))

My husband love's sausage gravy so I try to make it once a month or so.  I find it easier to leave the sausage in the pan after it is done cooking, along with the drippings.  I don't add any butter. I just sprinkle the flour in with the sausage slowly stirring until all of the flour is absorbed.  Then I add 2 cups of milk and simmer until thickened.  It always works.  I usually use 1% or 2% milk because we like the gravy thinner.  This is so quick and easy.

This is one of the best recipes for sausage gravy I have seen. I usually use a spicy hot sausage instead of maple, but it would be worth giving maple a try.  There is no reason to take the sausage out of the pan.  Browning the flour is essential, one reason restaurant gravy is so bland, they don't brown the flour.  I use enough flour to soak up the drippings, add salt and pepper, brown, and then add enough milk to make it the right consistancy.

This is close to my usual sausage gravy, with a two/three changes.  1)  I do not remove the sausage...just sprinkle the flour, and whisk for a few minutes....but do not allow it to start to brown. 2)  I use evaporated fat free milk.  Started doing this to make it easier for camping, and found it improved the entire dish.  This will also lower the calories.  3) For an everyday/week-end gravy I use turkey breakfast sausage.  It make it more healthy, and allows us to enjoy more frequently.  For special occasions -- maple is the way to go!

My husband is the biscuits and gravy connoisseur in our family.  He said this was excellent, but not quite to the outstanding level.  However, he also added, "Feel free to continue making this recipe 'often' while you work out what little thing is missing!" :o)--UPDATE--Here is what he says makes it the "world's best".  I use regular Jimmy Dean sausage and follow the directions exactly.  Then, I add two pinches of cayenne pepper, 60 twists of freshly ground black pepper (from a McCormick disposable shaker), and a swirl of maple syrup just before letting it simmer.  Delicious!  Of course, the thing that puts it right over the top is fresh, homemade biscuits!

country:
None
text:
This recipe is the Real Deal, except that I've always used "original" sausage.  The sausage should be removed while browning the flour, because it takes TIME to make a roux like this.  This step is NOT get rid of the pasty flour taste.  That will happen effortlessly during the simmering period!  What Bill's doing--and we should be, too--is SLOWLY BROWNING the flour, stirring often to prevent burning.  If you leave the sausage in throughout this process, the sausage gets overcooked, and you won't be able to tell when the flour becomes "light brown." Browning the flour adds tremendous flavor, just as browning meat does, but you can't do it fast.  Sure, you can stir the flour around a little and then add the milk, but it won't be the same gravy.  Personally, I like the gravy BOTH ways, "white" and "brown," but Bill specifically says to cook the flour "until light brown."  And the picture seems to confirm that he did.  You're right, Bill, this IS the best!

This was excellent.  While browning the sausage, I mixed the flour and about 1 cup of the milk in a shaker. I make this sausage gravy all the time. I only use regular sausage though. I don't even bother to remove the meat from the pan. After the meat is pretty much cooked through, I throw the butter(if it needs it) and the flour in the pan and finish browning it all together. When the flour is golden brown add your milk, adding more until desired thickness. Add salt and pepper or any other seasonings to taste. Wonderful!!!

text:
Amazingly simple to make and basically fool proof! Tried with multiple variations but came downtown to overall best in my opinion was: 
-Subbing the sausage with 1/2 maple sausage and 1/2 spicy sausage....gives it just the right amount of sweetness with a little kick of spiciness. *play with the ratio of maple and spicy sausage to fit your tastebuds....ie: for more sweeter gravy use more maple sausage.
-Leaving the ground sausage in its drippings to make the roux, then adding the milk slowly and using the back of the tablespoon to help mix and mush the roux with the milk forming smoothest gravy
-I feel the slower you go with this gravy the tastier it becomes....it allows all the flavors to merry together quite nicely. 

Never again with sausage gravy will I go back to mixing my flour and milk then pouring over the sausage to mix and serve....so splendidly ecstatic to have found this recipe!

Read the recipe, had to try right then. Didn't have maple (wish I had & next time will) used 8 thawed patties. Pretty much followed recipe to a T. After you add flour you need to stir constantly, and when it starts to turn brown, does so quick, keep an eye on it. Right before the simmer part I did add:

1/8 tsp onion powder,
1/8 tsp garlic powder,
pinch of cayenne (bout half an 1/8) don't really like spicy hot,
heaping 1/8 tsp oregano,
1/4 tsp parsley flakes,
1/4 tsp pepper,
1/8 tsp salt, lord knows there is enough sodium in everything we eat, and
right before serving...3/4 - 1 tbsp chives.....

Scrambled a couple eggs, put on the biscuits, and YES MA'AM, YOU ARE WELCOME. My Memaw would be proud.

text:
This basic recipe is how I've made my gravy for years. However, I use sage or a combination of sage and spicy flavored sausage, never use butter (it's rich enough,) and I just add the flour right onto the sausage without removing it from the skillet first, cooking it for a few minutes before adding the milk, it's quicker. Sometimes I saut minced onion along with the sausage and since I don't like big chunks of meat I use a pastry blender to break up the pieces just before I add the flour. A generous helping of fresh ground pepper and a splash of heavy cream and your guests will be licking their plates and begging for more!

text:
I've tried Maple, but we prefer the hot sausage.  Brown the sausage with some grated onions, if you like them.  Add the flour directly over the sausage and stir and brown the flour.  It will mix up on the sausage and use the oil from the sausage as well.  If you need more fat, add  1 T. of Olive oil and 1 T. butter. Pepper with fresh ground, quite heavily.  Bake the biscuits, I always like to split them and butter, but some prefer them whole.  While the biscuits are baking, add 2 to 3 cans of evaporated milk from the can and at least one can of water to keep it still thin enough to put on the gravy and not just globs. You can add salt at the table, if you really need it, and more black pepper or red sauce.  Enjoy.  Been making this forever.

text:
Though this is ok my version has less fat, tastes just as good and is less work.  1 lb sausage of your choice, we like 'Hot' pork sausage, 2 heaping Tbs. flour or 3Tbs. gluten free alternative flour mix (like Pamela's brand),1 can evaporated milk (reg or skim), salt and pepper or additional seasonings to taste and additional fresh whole milk as needed.
Brown sausage well on medium high heat until you have browned bits on the bottom of the pan-cast iron works best. Stir in flour (w/o removing the sausage) and let it cook a few minutes stirring occasionally. Add canned milk while stirring and bring to a boil.  Once boil has been reached and gravy has thickened taste, adjust seasonings as needed and add additional milk if it gets too thick or you need to stretch the servings out or like less sausage in your gravy.  Enjoy.

text:
Wow this recipe has me floored! Soooo good!!!

I grew up in the South but live in NJ now.  It is IMPOSSIBLE to find sausage gravy in this part of the country.  sigh.

I decided to make this for my mom (another Southern gal) for Mother's Day.  Some tips and adjustments below:

-Def use a cast iron pan.  It's like flavor x 3!

-"sweet" sausage gravy sounded weird to me so instead of maple I picked up Hot sausage instead - Jimmy Dean brand and used 3/4 of the package.  I bet this tastes just as good with Sage flavored sausage.

-I know it's just flour but King Arthur Organic is superior.  $2.89 for a small package but you will absolutely notice the difference between  high quality product )organic or not) and a regular one.

-I measured out 3 cups of milk but whisked in a little at a time, adding more when the texture got too thick during cooking.   In the end I was left with about 1/3 cup.  

I can't believe I waited so many years to try making one of my top 5 favorite foods!!  I was going to be extra special and make homemade biscuits too but wanted everything to be perfect for my mom.  So I decided to stick with what I know and spread the gravy out on Pillsbury "southern style" biscuits instead.   Delicious - and super filling!!!    This one is a keeper!

text:
A good 'core-recipe'. Thank you. Have been making this with moose sausage in recent years. It tastes great, but moose tends to need some fat to brown nicely, even as sausage. Butter doesn't like the heat from browning, so I use bacon grease if I've got it and a high-smoke-point oil if I don't. (I omit the butter when I do this as it isn't needed.) If you try this, watch the salt when seasoning your gravy; bacon grease is quite salty. A half teaspoon (more/less to taste) of sage adds variety, too. YMMV

text:
Simple and fantastic.  How could anything with 50g of fat per serving not be delicious!  I use sagey breakfast sausage instead of maple.  Add a dash or two of tabasco at the end- you won't be able to taste hot sauce, but the vinegar and cayenne will make the sausage flavors pop.  To get rid of the flour taste, simmer longer.  Anything thickened with a white roux should simmer for 30 minutes stirring often.  If you can taste flour, the sauce is not done.  You may have to add additional milk as the sauce will continue to thicken while simmering.

Very Impressed. I used to have Biscuits and Gravy with Sunday breakfast at a certain restaurant in Phoenix. Now that i'm in Australia i obviously can't get it. 
This recipe is just as good. I followed the directions to the letter and came up with a wonderfully thick and rich sausage gravy. Your choice of sausage is going to be the telling factor depending on what flavours you want to achieve. My butcher gave me a good sausage meat that had virtually no fat which was wonderful, so i did need the butter. Then i added the salt and pepper dead last after i gave all the ingredients a chance to blend all the flavours together. 
I made fresh homemade biscuits (scones) to go with it and my neighbour and i are loving it. Thank you very much for giving me a wonderful recipe and a little taste of home.

text:
I've made sausage gravy like this for over 40 years and is the way I prepare it most of the time. Another option would be to fry the sausage, drain the grease add milk to deglaze the pan, heat to simmer and thicken with a cornstarch slurry. Fewer calories and a different (good smooth) texture. Add salt and pepper to taste when thick. Though I use original mild bulk sausage as we don't care for the maple flavor.

text:
Great recipe.  I cook hot sausage with some red pepper flakes and fresh cracked pepper. Drain fat.  Sprinkle about 2 Tablespoons Wondra (found in the flour isle in a blue cardboard can) on the sausage.  Cook for 1 to 2 minutes on medium.  Add milk to the degree of thickness you desire.  This reduces the fat and calories.  I leave the salt out to reduce sodium, there is plenty in the sausage.  Judy

text:
I make this for family & it can't be beat. For church however I add butter to the sausage drippings to equal 1-1/2 cup total, then add 1 tbsp. each of salt & pepper, 2 cups flour, a gallon of whole milk & 3lbs. sausage(I use locally packed regular mild & add 1/2 tsp. sage while browning). Cook as directed above. Makes 1-1/2 gallons. 
If you have any leftovers it freezes well. If it's become to thick just add a little milk or water to thawed gravy and whisk well.

This is a great simple recipe! I will make again. I did not have maple sausage, so I used jimmy Dean & squirted about a TBS of maple syrup into it during browing process to add the taste of sweet. I used 2% milk, to be a tad healthier..you would never know, I used fresh black pepper as well as a little white pepper. text:
I had some problems making this (not the recipe's fault) so I had to adapt and it STILL turned out fantastic.  First, there was no maple sausage at the grocery store. I bought sage sausage instead.  Secondly, there were almost NO drippings when the sausage was cooked. (What's up with that???) With no drippings, I had a dilemma. I added the butter directly to the crumbled sausage in the pan and cooked that for a little bit.  I then whisked together the milk and flour and added it directly to the pan.  Much to my surprise, the flavor and consistency still turned out great, easily the best sausage gravy I've ever made!  I'm really looking forward to trying this recipe as-written (which was my intention) but even with these alterations it was still easy and amazingly good.  Thanks!

Display Name:
MyTurnToCook
isPro:

photo:
https://images.media-allrecipes.com/userphotos/50x50/6229350.jpg
city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
I love this recipe. Since my father-in-law needs to watch his fat intake, I modified the recipe to cut a lot of the fat out.  I use turkey breakfast sausage and add a couple of tablespoons of maple syrup as the turkey sausage is cooking. You can add some dry sage if you like to kick it up a notch. I make sure to get the sausage nice and brown and then remove to a small bowl, leaving the drippings in the pan.  I add three tablespoons of Smart Balance 50/50 butter blend and melt, adding in the flour and whisking the roux for at least a minute to remove flour taste.  Instead of three cups of whole milk, I use two cups of Land 'O Lakes Fat Free half and half, and one cup of skim milk.  I add only the first cup of milk, whisk really well, then add the rest of the milk, seasoning well with salt and pepper. Now you've got all the taste without all the fat.  Totally yummy!

text:
My great grandmother made this gravy years before I was born .. and this has passed down thru the generations. 
Other variations are.. you can use any sausage that you prefer.. altho personally I like the sausage with sage. I've also used ham sausage it's just as good. 
Another use for the gravy is .. leave the sausage out completely and use bacon drippings ( don't we all have some we save )... anyway when completed use the gravy on boiled/fried poatatoes.. Yummy,,, for those of us that are short on milk another variation is use half water add alittle butter & garlic salt for flavor . We called it poor man's gravy then. It's just as good.

text:
I've follow this sausage gravy recipe over 100 times the past few decades.   I don't look at the process as its too simple.   Sometimes I add garlic and crushed red pepper when I cook the sausage to change it up.   Also I've sub'ed bacon grease (1tbls) for butter.   Don't worry about getting all of the sausage out either, sometimes I'm just lazy and put the butter in the pan with sausage, toss the flour in blend it up and heat it till I see a slight browning of the flour and add the milk.

Just a note.  You don't need to remove the sausage.  You really don't need the butter, but it's a good addition.  You can just sprinkle the flour over the sausage and stir in. The fat in the sausage will absorb the flour.  Then add the milk as called for and it will thicken perfectly.

The only sausage I had was frozen turkey sausage. So I thawed it and used that. I was always afraid that gravy was too hard to make, but I now realize it is: Hot fat/oil then mix in flour until it thickens then mix in milk until you have enough gravy then stir until it thickens again. Then season it... pretty simple. And for all the teachers out there who always wanted your students to sum up what they learned after the lesson here it is. I was listening in class.

text:
My whole life I thought I didn't like sausage gravy because my mother, bless her heart, wasn't the world's greatest cook. But this recipe changed my mind. I use regular sage breakfast sausage and I don't bother removing it from the pan before I add the butter and flour and use 2% milk; it thickens just fine. The key is lots and lots of fresh-ground pepper. When you think you've added enough, add more. I serve it over homemade sourdough biscuits (my great-grandmother's recipe) and it's the ultimate comfort food.

A-MAZING! I do use the breakfast sausage recipe found on this site (http://allrecipes.com/recipe/16359/breakfast-sausage/), and double the meat recipe for 2lbs of pork. I also add a bit of sage to the gravy recipe, for additional seasoning.

Whisk the flour into the milk, and add the combination to the drippings/butter. Stir constantly until it thickens up. I do keep a bit of thickening agent (either flour or corn starch) handy, to get it to the gravy-like consistency we like.  Excellent recipe!!!!

country:
None
text:
This recipe was good. Simplistic ingredients, and easy to make. The only advice I can offer is to resist the temptation to use the entire chub of sausage. Most chubs are 16oz i.e. Jimmy Dean. I thought to myself...'just use the whole thing'....so I did. That was a mistake. It's just too much sausage, and what happens is the gravy seemingly gets absorbed into the meat, and you lose that nice velvety gravy flow spilling over your biscuits and running onto the plate.  Trust me, 12oz will be enough. Use your favorite variety of sausage i.e. maple, sage, original, and you will enjoy. I added a sprinkle of cayenne pepper to mine.

One of my favorites for certain. The Maple sausage is a nice touch, but any breakfast sausage will work changing the taste of your gravy depending on the sausage. The type and brand of sausage you choose can make a big difference in taste or how spicy or bland your gravy turns out. Using butter in the recipe can be optional also, most sausage has ample grease to make a good gravy on it's own without adding butter.

text:
I think I've nailed this down at the firehouse.  1/4 cup butter (maybe a little more ;) 
1/4 cup flour 
2 cups milk, any
1 tube Sage breakfast sausage 
Salt
Black pepper
Crushed red pepper (a dash or two, don't go crazy)
Garlic powder (see above)
Slowly, melt butter and whisk in flour, then slowly whisk in milk. 
Brown meat at same time. 
Pour in browned meat,  simmer until thickened. 
BOOM!  Best sausage gravy, ever.

text:
I have made biscuits and gravy for years!  I never knew there was an actual recipe for it though.  I use regular sausage instead of the maple flavor and I don't add the butter, I just use the fat in the pan from browning the sausage.  Cook it up sprinkle flour evenly over the top and then start stirring in milk until well blended, I just eyeball it.  Once it heats up it starts to thicken up.  If it gets too thick I just add more milk; too thin and I let it bubble for a few minutes and it thickens right up.  I play with it until I get the consistency I want.  Easy-peasy!  I always serve with scrambled eggs.  We pour the gravy over the biscuits and over the scrambled eggs too!  YUM!

text:
This recipe was a good starting point for me, but if I made it just the way the recipe said, we wouldn't have enjoyed it very much. I accidentally used a pan that was larger than needed so I ended up adding quite a bit more milk than this called for. Once I got the white gravy the way I wanted it, I added lots of a pepper spice mix (Wildtree's Rancher Steak Rub) that I have in a spice grinder, garlic powder and seasoning salt. Even with all the pepper mix I added we thought it could have used a bit more. We just aren't bland food people so I'm glad I added more spices to it, but it was still so much better than anything we'd get eating out - we loved it!

city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
The reason some of you are getting a floury tasting gravy, is because you aren't allowing the flour and grease (roux) to cook enough. The recipe says "until smooth." From personal experience, any kind of roux should be cooked until it resembles the texture of sand, (for white gravy, without allowing it to brown). If it starts to brown, add the milk immediately. If you do this, it wont have a floury taste.

Not a huge fan of sausage so I went looking for a gravy that used bacon but did not find one.  I decided to make this one using bacon.   I fried about half a package of bacon and set aside the actual bacon.  I poured 3/4ths of the bacon grease into a tin leaving the remaining one third in the pan. I then followed the recipe exactly as noted except for I crumbled the bacon into the gravy when the recipe called to stir in sausage.  I then added more bacon grease as needed for flavor.  My boyfriend loved it and I agree it was good.  Next time i am going to try maple flavored bacon.

text:
This is essentially the same as the recipe I've used for years, except I omit the butter to avoid the extra fat and you don't really have to remove the sausage.  Just mix in flour with sausage once the sausage is completely cooked.  Stir around completely until sausage is completely coated and all grease is soaked up.  Then, add milk, sage, black pepper, and cayenne pepper and cook until thickness you desire is achieved.  If not enough gravy, add more milk and continue cooking until thickness is achieved and pour over hot biscuits or toast (SOS).  Excellent.

Nice, simple recipe.  I doubled it to serve at a Sunday Brunch and it turned out just fine.  I actually made the gravy about 1 1/2 hours before Brunch, covered it, and set it aside.  I reheated the gravy right before serving and it held up beautifully.  I used regular sausage, instead of maple-flavored, but otherwise stuck to the original recipe.  For those who complain about blandness, this is not supposed to be a highly seasoned dish.  Just look at the ingredients.  People tend to adjust the seasoning using as much salt and pepper as they wish at the table.  Thanks, Bill - this is a keeper!
